Main category: astro-ph.CO

TL;DR: The paper evaluates the validity of cluster clustering (CC) models for template-fitting, which will be used to analyze the anisotropy of the redshift-space two-point correlation function (2PCF) from the Euclid satellite's galaxy cluster catalog. The study uses semi-analytic simulations and tests three clustering models under realistic and optimistic photometric redshift uncertainty scenarios, finding that the dispersion model provides unbiased inferences on $fσ_8$ down to 10 $h^{-1}$ Mpc for a DR1-like setting.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The motivation is to assess the validity of cluster clustering (CC) models for template-fitting, which will complement the full-shape methodology in providing cosmological information from the anisotropy of the redshift-space two-point correlation function (2PCF). This is important for the analysis of the upcoming \textit{Euclid} satellite's galaxy cluster catalog, which will cover a large area of the sky.\n\n动机是评估用于模板拟合的星系团聚类（CC）模型的有效性，这将补充全形状方法，从红移空间两点相关函数（2PCF）的各向异性中提供宇宙学信息。这对于即将发布的\textit{Euclid}卫星的星系团目录分析非常重要，该目录将覆盖大面积的天空。

Method: The method involves using the semi-analytic \code{PINOCCHIO} code with third-order Lagrangian perturbation theory to simulate the two-point redshift-space clustering of galaxy clusters. The simulation assumes a \textit{Euclid} DR1-like footprint. The first three even multipoles of the 2PCF and the associated covariance matrix are estimated from 1000 synthetic catalogues. Three clustering models (dispersion, Scoccimarro, and Taruya--Nishimichi--Saito) are applied to mock catalogues, and the impact of nonlinearities, halo bias, and photometric redshift uncertainties is studied. The models are validated against 100 mock catalogues via inference of the growth rate times the matter power spectrum normalization parameter, $fσ_8$.\n\n方法包括使用半解析的\code{PINOCCHIO}代码和三阶拉格朗日扰动理论来模拟星系团的两点红移空间聚类。模拟假设了一个\textit{Euclid} DR1类的足迹。从1000个合成目录中估计了2PCF的前三个偶极子及其相关的协方差矩阵。将三种聚类模型（色散、Scoccimarro 和 Taruya--Nishimichi--Saito）应用于模拟目录，并研究了非线性、晕偏置和光度红移不确定性的影响。通过推断增长率乘以物质功率谱归一化参数$fσ_8$，用100个模拟目录验证了这些模型。

Result: The results show that the dispersion model, the simplest of the three, yields unbiased inferences on $fσ_8$ down to 10 $h^{-1}$ Mpc in a DR1-like setting. All clustering models provide very similar goodness-of-fit metrics in the presence of DR1-like cluster redshift uncertainties.\n\n结果显示，在DR1类设置下，最简单的色散模型在10 $h^{-1}$ Mpc尺度上对$fσ_8$提供了无偏推断。在存在DR1类星系团红移不确定性的情况下，所有聚类模型都提供了非常相似的拟合优度指标。

Conclusion: The conclusion is that the dispersion model is a viable option for analyzing the anisotropy of the redshift-space 2PCF from the \textit{Euclid} satellite's galaxy cluster catalog, as it provides unbiased inferences on $fσ_8$ down to 10 $h^{-1}$ Mpc. The other clustering models also perform well, but the simplicity of the dispersion model makes it a preferred choice for the analysis.\n\n结论是，色散模型是分析\textit{Euclid}卫星星系团目录中红移空间2PCF各向异性的可行选择，因为它在10 $h^{-1}$ Mpc尺度上对$fσ_8$提供了无偏推断。其他聚类模型也表现良好，但由于色散模型的简单性，使其成为分析的首选。

Abstract: The \textit{Euclid} satellite will deliver a catalogue of optically-selected galaxy clusters spanning from around $2000$ deg$^2$ in Data Release (DR) 1 to around $14\,000$ deg$^2$ in DR3. We assess the validity of cluster clustering (CC) models for template-fitting, which complements the full-shape methodology in providing cosmological information from the anisotropy of the redshift-space two-point correlation function (2PCF). Both will be used to analyse the cluster 2PCF multipoles in \textit{Euclid}. We analyse the multipoles of the two-point redshift-space clustering of galaxy clusters simulated with the semi-analytic \code{PINOCCHIO} code using third-order Lagrangian perturbation theory, assuming a \textit{Euclid} DR1-like footprint of 500 deg$^2$ in the Northern Hemisphere and 1400 deg$^2$ in the Southern Hemisphere. We estimate the first three even multipoles of the 2PCF and associated covariance matrix from 1000 DR1-like synthetic catalogues. We study the impact of the modelling of nonlinearities, halo bias, and photometric redshift uncertainties on the 2PCF. We apply three clustering models to the mock catalogues at $0<z<2$ and virial mass $M_{\rm vir}>10^{14}\;h^{-1}\,M_\odot$ under realistic and optimistic photometric redshift uncertainty scenarios. We formulate a set of permissive and conservative criteria that should be fulfilled by the multipole cut-off scales and validate against 100 mock catalogues via inference of the growth rate times the matter power spectrum normalisation parameter, $fσ_8$. We test the dispersion, Scoccimarro, and Taruya--Nishimichi--Saito models. We find that the simplest of the three -- the dispersion model -- yields unbiased inferences on $fσ_8$ from CC down to $10$ $h^{-1}$ Mpc in a DR1-like setting. All clustering models provide very similar goodness-of-fit metrics in the presence of DR1-like cluster redshift uncertainties.

### [90] [Substructure in redMaPPer clusters and its impact on X-ray morphology and scaling relations](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.25770)
*R. Tuomainen,A. Finoguenov,J. Comparat,L. Doubrawa*

TL;DR: The paper quantifies the prevalence and properties of substructure in optical galaxy clusters using HDBSCAN on the redMaPPer catalog, correlates these with X-ray morphological parameters from eROSITA, and analyzes the scaling relation between X-ray luminosity and optical richness. It finds that 40% of clusters have substructure, which is correlated with disturbed X-ray morphologies, especially in high-mass clusters, and influences the Lx-lambda relation's scatter evolution.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The motivation is to understand the impact of substructure in galaxy clusters on their X-ray morphology and scaling relations, specifically how substructure affects the X-ray luminosity and its relationship with optical richness. The study aims to provide a statistical analysis of substructure and its correlation with X-ray properties, which can help in understanding the dynamics and evolution of galaxy clusters.

动机是理解星系团中的次结构对其X射线形态和标度关系的影响，特别是次结构如何影响X射线光度及其与光学丰富度的关系。该研究旨在提供次结构的统计分析及其与X射线性质的相关性，这有助于理解星系团的动力学和演化。

Method: The method involves applying the hierarchical density-based clustering algorithm HDBSCAN to the redMaPPer galaxy cluster catalog to identify and characterize substructure. The identified substructures are then cross-matched with the eROSITA X-ray morphology catalog to correlate optical substructure with X-ray morphological parameters. Finally, the scaling relation between X-ray luminosity and optical richness is analyzed for clusters with and without substructure.

方法包括将基于层次密度的聚类算法HDBSCAN应用于redMaPPer星系团目录以识别和表征次结构。然后将识别出的次结构与eROSITA X射线形态目录进行交叉匹配，以关联光学次结构与X射线形态参数。最后，对于有和没有次结构的星系团，分析X射线光度与光学丰富度之间的标度关系。

Result: The results show that approximately 40% of the clusters have substructure, with a quarter of the full sample having a fractional contribution to richness in excess of 35%. There is a significant correlation between optical substructure and disturbed X-ray morphologies, particularly in high-mass clusters. Clusters with substructure also exhibit a stronger redshift evolution in the scatter of the Lx-lambda relation, with lower-redshift clusters displaying higher X-ray luminosity at fixed richness compared to relaxed systems.

结果表明，大约40%的星系团具有次结构，其中四分之一的样本对丰富度的贡献超过35%。光学次结构与扰动的X射线形态之间存在显著相关性，特别是在高质量星系团中。具有次结构的星系团在Lx-lambda关系的散度上表现出更强的红移演化，在固定丰富度的情况下，低红移星系团比松弛系统显示出更高的X射线光度。

Conclusion: The conclusion is that substructure in galaxy clusters significantly affects their X-ray properties, leading to more disturbed X-ray morphologies and a stronger redshift evolution in the scatter of the Lx-lambda relation. This suggests that mergers and substructure play a crucial role in the dynamical state and evolution of galaxy clusters, with the effects being more pronounced at lower redshifts due to the increased density contrast and longer survival times of substructures.

结论是星系团中的次结构显著影响其X射线性质，导致更扰动的X射线形态以及Lx-lambda关系散度的更强红移演化。这表明合并和次结构在星系团的动力学状态和演化中起着关键作用，由于次结构的密度对比增加和生存时间延长，这些效应在较低红移时更为明显。

Abstract: We statistically quantified the prevalence and properties of substructure in optical galaxy clusters and directly investigated its impact on X-ray morphology and scaling relations, leveraging new data from the DECaLS Legacy Survey and the SRG/eROSITA all-sky survey. We applied the hierarchical density-based clustering algorithm HDBSCAN to the redMaPPer galaxy cluster catalog to identify and characterize substructure from the probabilistic membership assignments. We then cross-matched this sample with the eROSITA X-ray morphology catalog to correlate optical substructure with a comprehensive set of X-ray morphological parameters. Finally, we analyzed the scaling relation between X-ray luminosity and optical richness for clusters with and without substructure. Substructure is a common feature, present in approximately 40% of clusters; a quarter of the full sample exhibits a fractional contribution to richness in excess of 35%. We find a highly significant correlation between optical substructure and disturbed X-ray morphologies, a trend that is strongest for high-mass clusters. The clusters with substructure also drive a stronger redshift evolution in the scatter of the Lx-lambda relation. At low redshifts (z<0.2), they display a systematically higher X-ray luminosity at fixed richness compared to relaxed systems. We attribute the enhanced effect of mergers on X-ray properties at low redshifts to the increased density contrast of low-redshift cool cores and longer substructure survival times, which are possibly due to the suppression of disruptive mixing by effects such as magnetic draping. At lower cluster richness, a discordance between X-ray morphology and the merging state indicates a growing relative importance of active galactic nucleus feedback in governing X-ray morphology.

</details>


### [91] [Geometric Constraints on the Pre-Recombination Expansion History from the Hubble Tension](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.25813)
*Davide Pedrotti*

Main category: astro-ph.CO

TL;DR: A model-independent reconstruction of the pre-recombination expansion history suggests that early-time enhancements in the expansion rate, specifically around a 15% increase, can resolve the Hubble tension while being consistent with CMB data. This finding provides a foundation for future model development and testing of Hubble tension proposals.\n\n对再结合前膨胀历史的模型无关重构表明，早期膨胀率的增加（特别是大约15%的增加）可以在与CMB数据一致的情况下解决哈勃张力。这一发现为未来模型开发和哈勃张力提案的测试提供了基础。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The motivation is to explore whether there are purely early-time solutions to the Hubble tension that can be consistent with the observed CMB data. The aim is to provide a framework for understanding the possible modifications to the early universe's expansion history that could alleviate the Hubble tension.\n\n动机是探索是否存在纯粹的早期宇宙解决方案来缓解哈勃张力，同时与观测到的CMB数据保持一致。目的是提供一个框架，以理解可能对早期宇宙膨胀历史进行的修改，从而缓解哈勃张力。

Method: The method involves a model-independent reconstruction of the background pre-recombination expansion history of the Universe. The analysis is based on satisfying the geometric CMB constraints and identifying the necessary conditions for resolving the Hubble tension at early times.\n\n该方法涉及对宇宙再结合前背景膨胀历史的模型无关重构。分析基于满足几何CMB约束，并确定在早期解决哈勃张力所需的条件。

Result: The result shows that there exist purely early-time resolutions to the Hubble tension, which involve a $\simeq 15\%$ enhancement in the expansion rate before recombination, with a smooth transition around matter-radiation equality. These findings highlight the potential for early-universe modifications to address the Hubble tension without invoking late-time physics.\n\n结果显示，存在纯早期宇宙的哈勃张力解决方案，这些方案涉及在再结合之前的膨胀率增加约15%，并在物质-辐射等效时期有一个平滑的过渡。这些发现突出了通过早期宇宙修改来解决哈勃张力的可能性，而无需诉诸晚期宇宙物理。

Conclusion: The study concludes that there are purely early-time resolutions to the Hubble tension at the background level, which require a smooth transition around matter-radiation equality with an expansion rate enhancement of approximately 15% prior to recombination. This result provides a blueprint for future model-building and a background stress-test for Hubble tension proposals.\n\n该研究得出结论，存在纯早期宇宙的哈勃张力解决方案，这些方案在背景水平上满足几何CMB约束。这类解决方案要求在物质-辐射等效时期有一个平滑的过渡，其特征是在再结合之前膨胀率增强约15%。这一结果为未来的模型构建提供了蓝图，并为哈勃张力提案提供了一个背景压力测试。

Abstract: I perform a model-independent reconstruction of the background pre-recombination expansion history of the Universe. I find that purely early-time resolutions to the Hubble tension, satisfying the geometric CMB constraints, exist at the background level. This class of solutions requires a smooth transition around matter-radiation equality, characterized by a $\simeq 15\%$ expansion rate enhancement prior to recombination. This result serves as a blueprint for future model-building approaches, providing a background stress-test for Hubble tension proposals.

### [92] [Fast radio burst dispersion is an unbiased tracer of matter on large scales](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.25828)
*Shion Andrew,Haochen Wang,Kiyoshi Masui,Josh Borrow,Calvin Leung,Ryan Raikman,Matthieu Schaller,Joop Schaye,James M. Sullivan*

Main category: astro-ph.CO

TL;DR: The paper discusses the use of fast radio bursts (FRBs) as an unbiased tracer of the matter distribution on large scales, leveraging the dispersion of FRBs to measure the column density of free electrons. The authors show that the electron bias can be constrained at the percent level and that a significant number of localized FRBs can match the statistical power of weak-lensing measurements, making FRB dispersion a new, independent method for tracing matter.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The motivation is to establish fast radio bursts (FRBs) as a reliable and unbiased tracer of the matter distribution in the universe. By measuring the dispersion of FRBs, which is related to the column density of free electrons, the study aims to trace the diffuse ionized gas that constitutes over 90% of all baryons. This approach leverages baryon-mass conservation, which ensures that the total baryon field has a unit linear bias, with the dispersion inheriting this bias up to small corrections from stellar and neutral-gas components. [English Text]
The motivation is to establish fast radio bursts (FRBs) as a reliable and unbiased tracer of the matter distribution in the universe. By measuring the dispersion of FRBs, which is related to the column density of free electrons, the study aims to trace the diffuse ionized gas that constitutes over 90% of all baryons. This approach leverages baryon-mass conservation, which ensures that the total baryon field has a unit linear bias, with the dispersion inheriting this bias up to small corrections from stellar and neutral-gas components. [Chinese Text]

Method: The method involves using existing galaxy and 21 cm surveys to bound the corrections from stellar and neutral-gas components at the percent level. The FLAMINGO hydrodynamical simulations are used to confirm that the electron bias varies at the percent level across different feedback prescriptions. The dispersion-galaxy cross-power spectrum at linear scales is analyzed to constrain $B_8 \equiv σ_8(Ω_b/0.05)^{1/2}$, a baryonic analog of $S_8$. [English Text]
The method involves using existing galaxy and 21 cm surveys to bound the corrections from stellar and neutral-gas components at the percent level. The FLAMINGO hydrodynamical simulations are used to confirm that the electron bias varies at the percent level across different feedback prescriptions. The dispersion-galaxy cross-power spectrum at linear scales is analyzed to constrain $B_8 \equiv σ_8(Ω_b/0.05)^{1/2}$, a baryonic analog of $S_8$. [Chinese Text]

Result: The results show that the electron bias can be constrained at the percent level using current data, and the FLAMINGO simulations confirm that the electron bias varies only slightly across different feedback models. The dispersion-galaxy cross-power spectrum provides a direct constraint on $B_8$, which is independent of feedback physics. Additionally, it is shown that about $10^5$ localized FRBs can provide a statistical power comparable to that of $10^8$ weak-lensing galaxy shape measurements. [English Text]
The results show that the electron bias can be constrained at the percent level using current data, and the FLAMINGO simulations confirm that the electron bias varies only slightly across different feedback models. The dispersion-galaxy cross-power spectrum provides a direct constraint on $B_8$, which is independent of feedback physics. Additionally, it is shown that about $10^5$ localized FRBs can provide a statistical power comparable to that of $10^8$ weak-lensing galaxy shape measurements. [Chinese Text]

Conclusion: The conclusion is that the dispersion of fast radio bursts (FRBs) can serve as a new, unbiased tracer of the matter distribution on large scales, similar to weak lensing and redshift-space distortions. The study demonstrates that the electron bias is stable and can be constrained at the percent level, and that a significant number of localized FRBs can match the statistical power of weak-lensing measurements. [English Text]
The conclusion is that the dispersion of fast radio bursts (FRBs) can serve as a new, unbiased tracer of the matter distribution on large scales, similar to weak lensing and redshift-space distortions. The study demonstrates that the electron bias is stable and can be constrained at the percent level, and that a significant number of localized FRBs can match the statistical power of weak-lensing measurements. [Chinese Text]

Abstract: The dispersion of fast radio bursts (FRBs) measures the column density of free electrons, tracing the diffuse ionized gas that contains more than $90\%$ of all baryons. On linear scales the FRB dispersion field is an approximately unbiased tracer of the matter distribution, an idea long assumed in the FRB large-scale structure literature and recently formalized by Zhou and Zhang [arXiv:2510.11022]. This follows from baryon-mass conservation, which forces the total baryon field to have unit linear bias, with dispersion inheriting this bias up to small corrections from the stellar and neutral-gas components. We show these corrections can be bounded at the percent level using existing galaxy and 21 cm surveys, and confirm with the FLAMINGO hydrodynamical simulations that the electron bias varies at the percent level across a wide range of feedback prescriptions. The dispersion-galaxy cross-power spectrum at linear scales directly constrains $B_8 \equiv σ_8(Ω_b/0.05)^{1/2}$, a baryonic analog of $S_8$, independently of feedback physics. Because most of the per-object variance in dispersion is cosmological signal rather than noise, $\sim\!10^5$ localized FRBs can match the statistical power of $\sim\!10^8$ weak-lensing galaxy shape measurements. FRB dispersion thus joins weak lensing and redshift-space distortions as a new unbiased tracer of matter on large scales.

</details>
